<Rate>4<//Rate>< Text>
If you're hungry, for $15 you can eat your fill at this Asian buffet. Not fine dining, but filling. It's good, but not great. You come here for value. There are a few items that were really good, like the little sesame balls filled with red bean for dessert.

But over all, this is about filling up on the cheap. It was clean, quiet, the staff was friendly, and it's a pleasant experience for very little money. I basically gave it an extra star for value.< /Text>

<pictures>None</pictures>< Review>
Where do I even start. If I could give them 6 stars I would.  As soon as I walked in I was welcomed by the many people working there. They knew imdeietly what I wanted. The meal cost lest then $5 and it was amazing. They even went and made another batch of fried rice just for me. I sat down and began to eat and soon there was a steaming plate of fried rice in my face. I‚Äôve never gotten this much food for $5 ever. The fried rice had chunks of ham and juicy carrots in them while the sesame chicken had a nice crunchy outside with and extremely juicy inside. My water was always being refilled which was great and I even noticed that they took the time to organized the sugar packets on the tables. They people there were extremely nice to me and I expect to be eating there from here on out. Disregard any of the 1 star comment because they are completely not true. This place will serve you and the employees put their heart and soul into their job. It feels like they never go outside because they are so focused inside. Please go here often, this place is out of this world.<//Review>

<user_name>Jeanine Fetterly</user_name>< Date>
1536348152071</Date>
< rating>
2<//rating>
< review>
Came in for dinner about 6:00, assuming the food would  be fresh and hot at that time.  It was neither. I've read lots of reviews of this restaurant and it seems that it has more sentimental value than food quality. Many people comment that they had been coming for years and the place is as good as it gets. It's not! Perhaps these people should investigate the Chinese buffet at ninth and Broadway in Oakland, only a mile away. Or one on International Blvd or on Willow Pass in Concord. They are four times as large, much greater selection, includes free soft drinks and a 10% senior discount. The price is only two dollars more than they Genghis Khan, a much better value.

To be more specific, I found that their sushi to be excellent and the proper was Sasabi and pickled ginger was available.  Nothing on the rest of the buffet compared favorably. The wonton soup was mildly flavorful but the wonton skins were mushy as they had  seem to have been cooked over and over. At 6 o'clock, the beginning of the dinner hour, most of the food on the buffet was only room temperature. It advertises a" seafood buffet", yet the only fish was a single flat overcooked and very unappealing filet of fish with the skin on. The mussels and clams were flavorless. The oysters while large and in the shell were not raw, as is common on other Chinese buffets, but had a dense and strange texture. When I inquired I was told that indeed they were not fresh but had been steamed. They were not served with any sauce. Steamed oysters? They were dreadful. I was disappointed. And the shrimp served in the fried shell was shriveled and tasteless. There were no tempting vegetables at all, simply a pan of chopped bell pepper and celery with a few tiny cooked shrimp thrown in, again totally tasteless. The only 'appetizer' was egg rolls, cold and greasy.

As for condiments, I've never been to a Chinese restaurant or buffet where the condiments were not available on the individual tables. These were not and one had to dish them up in small plates and carry each to the table individually. What shocked me was a large bottle of Heinz ketchup on the condiment tray by the end of the buffet table. Ketchup in a Chinese restaurant??? I should have been forewarned when I came in and saw all the tables laid out only with knife and fork, no chopstick options. I guess people in Alameda prefer this rather bland and unpleasant preparation of food as there was not an Asian in the restaurant. They were all over in Oakland's Chinatown where the food is infinitely better.

On the plus side, I will say that the atmosphere was clean, cheery, pleasant, and the waitress was very attentive in clearing dishes and bringing fresh ice water.</review>

<Text>Can't beat it for the price.  I come in here for lunch. While the buffet food is not exquisite quality, when fresh it's as good as any asain buffet. What separates this place is the Mongolian bbq area. Since it's made to order it's always hot off the grill when it arrives to your table.  You get to decide what goes in and how to season it. It makes me laugh reading other reviews that state it (the Mongolian portion of service) lacks flavor.... guess those folks are not articulate in the culinary field...add more flavor (curry, ginger, garlic, satay, oyster, teriyaki, sweet n sour, soy sauce, Sriracha) if it lacks flavor! My first time coming to this place was awesome. Second time not so much. I walked in and approached the counter where an employee was waiting behind the counter. She made eye contact with me abd immediately walked into the back and proceeded to do frivelous tasks. Legit 3 minutes and never looked back at me or returned to take my order. In this entire transacation that took forever to just order, this woman still had not returned to the front. All the while laughing and cracking jokes in the back where i could still see her and she can see me. I hate pulling the race card bit i am a black woman, this employee is a latina woman. The employee that finally came to help me, was a black man. If it werent for him i may not have been served. I will not be bringing my money back to this broke down establishment ever again. Do not waste your time.</review>

< user_id>
105330578909981949868< /user_id>
<name>Ayisha Gabri<//name>< time>
1456465566587<//time>
<rating>4<//rating>< review>
Nice little place. It's tucked into strip mall next to Outback steakhouse. There's designated parking for Wings Empire customers only right up front. Nice little bonus BC Outback is always packed and taking up all the parking. The service was great the lady was super patient and answered all our questions. It was also CLEAN very CLEAN huge bonus.

Onto the food... They have a pretty good menu and prices are very reasonable. They offer more then just wings. They have some massive burgers and the regular fried food appetizers. They also have wraps that look really good to. I took the whole family so we ordered a few different items. My oldest daughter got the buffalo chicken fries (they offer them in small,med,large) she opted for medium BC she said she was starving. Well they were massive for a medium and she now has lunch and dinner for tomorrow. I stole a few bites and they were great. The fries fresh and hot and perfect amount of chicken and sauce. Highly recommend you try these. The other two split the $5.99 5 piece chicken tender and 3 bread stick combo with BBQ sauce. The chicken strips were very big. I was thinking for $5.99 they would be those little chicken finger things you get at some other places. Nope they were all very large moist pieces of chicken with just enough BBQ sauce. The bread sticks were fresh and hot with a nice sprinkling of parmesan cheese. They were a huge hit at the table. Wife and I got the 15 Wing and made it a combo. Came with 5 bread sticks and drink. We chose 3 flavors. Good old fashion medium Wing sauce. It was delicious with right amount of tang and heat. Second choice was tropical thunder. It was sweet with pineapple hint and a massive heat on the back end but not over powering. Definitely had us saying "what do you mean you people" sorry for cheesy pun I had to with that name. Last and by far the favorite was mango habanero. Such a sweet flavorful mango beginning and then the habanero comes in and joins the party and then finishes it!!!! Was so addicting and oh so hot but in a good way. Highly recommend trying them if you're a fan of the heat.

The cook and lady running register checked in on us and even brought food to the table. We even asked for an item that wasn't on the menu (was on the online menu) and the chef made it for my kids and didn't even charge us!!!! The only negative was that they didn't have a bathroom. But I can overlook that BC the service, quality and portion sizes make up for it. Will be back often.< /review>

< review>
My third time eating here and I gotta say I love it. It's built your own bowl just like Chipotle but Asian style. They use fresh ingredients, good quality meats and veggies. Their sauces are delicious, hard to chose which one to get. My favorite protein is the steak satay. (The chicken satay is good too.)
I normally get jasmine rice , steak or chicken satay, the peanut sauce and top it off with  lots of delicious sides.
Finding parking can be challenging on the weekends but you can always park at the Sprouts parking lot. The customer service isn't the greatest but will do.

Photo of TAP The Asian Project - Burbank, CA, United States</review>

It's a Chipotle for Asian bowls - very good.

Everything is made fresh in-house and it shows.  Creative toppings and fresh herbs like mint and cilantro.  A wide variety of sauces makes for a healthy and tasty meal.

< Review>
I lived in this Community for a year and all was ok including maintenance but when my apartment was up for renewal the management did not  even bother to send a notice with the renewal details. When I went to leasing office they said because of Covid situation they are not sending details for renewal and will put on month on month once the lease is over.
I wanted to connect with the property manager Ann but was not let to connect with her as she was very busy and was asked to communicate over mail. I dropped a mail for the renewal details and called the office regularly and sent reminders but only got a response from Ann after a week which said she can offer the new price for a 6 month lease only which I denied and asked for a 12 months lease. Again no reply for next 5 days and then when I found a new apartment which was much cheaper and better I put up a notice to vacate the place and within an hour I got a reply stating that the can offer me the lease for a year with the renewed rate. If they would have offered me earlier then mostly I would not have changed but anyways got a better apartment at a much cheaper rate.
And lastly forget your security deposit of $800 as Willowbend as they will put some junk changes and deduct your whole amount. My monthly utility in the 12 months that I had stayed had come a maximum of $120 a month but when I vacated the apartment it seems for a month and 10 days the amount is $308 which I am not sure how it was calculated. Also they put a cleaning charge, paint, carpet and every possible change when I had maintained the apartment well and did a full cleaning before leaving the apartment.
So I would suggest better stay away from this apartment and you won't get response from the management nor will you get back your security money of $800. Only good thing is there maintenance staff as they work promptly and resolve any service request raised with in 24 hours which is highly appreciable.</Review>

<Rate>5<//Rate><pics>None</pics><time>1611682387820<//time><review>Home of the lowest, hottest point in North America, giant yuccas, and moving stones.

North America‚Äôs smallest, driest desert is sandwiched between the cold Great Basin Desert to the north  and the hot Sonoran Desert to the south. Due to its proximity to two contrasting desert areas, experts rarely agree on the Mojave‚Äôs boundaries, size, or type.

Levels of extremes.
Badwater Basin in the Mojave‚Äôs Death Valley lies 282 ft (86 m) below sea level‚Äîthe continent‚Äôs lowest point‚Äî yet Telescope Peak in the Panamint Range soars  11,043 ft (3,366 m) above it. North America‚Äôs highest  air temperature of 134¬∞F (57¬∞C) was recorded here, at Furnace Creek in 1913, yet winter temperatures regularly drop below freezing. Winds above 50 mph (80 kph) often buffet the Mojave‚Äôs western edge but are rare in the east. In the north, low-growing scrubland resembles the Great Basin Desert, but to the south, creosote bush takes hold.
The Joshua tree, the largest North American yucca, is a symbol of the Mojave and is often used by ecologists as an indicator of the desert‚Äôs southern boundary. Death Valley is also home to ‚Äúsailing stones‚Äù‚Äîboulders that appear to move unaided (see panel, left).< /review>< gmap_id>

<text>The Mojave Desert is bordered by the¬†Great Basin Desert¬†to its north[5]¬†and the¬†Sonoran Desert¬†to its south and east.[5]¬†Topographical boundaries include the¬†Tehachapi Mountains¬†and the¬†Sierra Pelona Ridge¬†to the west, the¬†Sierra Nevada¬†and the¬†Inyo Mountains¬†to the northwest, and the¬†San Gabriel Mountains¬†and¬†San Bernardino Mountains¬†to the south. The mountain boundaries are distinct because they are outlined by the two largest faults in California ‚Äì the¬†San Andreas¬†and¬†Garlock¬†faults. The Mojave Desert displays typical¬†basin and range¬†topography. Higher elevations above 2,000¬†ft (610¬†m) in the Mojave are commonly referred to as the High Desert; however,¬†Death Valley¬†is the lowest elevation in North America at 280¬†ft (85¬†m) below sea level and is one of the Mojave Desert's harshest climates and best known places. Large parts of the Mojave Desert are often referred to as the "high desert", in contrast to the "low desert", the Sonoran Desert to the south. Most of the Mojave Desert is above 2,000¬†ft (610¬†m), with only Death Valley and the Colorado River basin in the east (including the neighboring Las Vegas Valley) being lower. The Mojave Desert, however, is generally lower than the even higher Great Basin Desert to the north. The Mojave Desert occupies less than 50,000 sq mi (130,000 km2), making it the smallest of the North American deserts.[5]<//text><pics>None</pics></record>

< Review>
The Mojave Desert (/mo äÀàh…ëÀêvi, m…ô-/ mo-HAH-vee)[2][3][4] is an arid rain-shadow desert and the driest desert in North America.[5] It is in the southwestern United States, primarily within southeastern California and southern Nevada, and it occupies 47,877 sq mi (124,000 km2). Very small areas also extend into Utah and Arizona.[6] Its boundaries are generally noted by the presence of Joshua trees, which are native only to the Mojave Desert and are considered an indicator species, and it is believed to support an additional 1,750 to 2,000 species of plants.[7] The central part of the desert is sparsely populated, while its peripheries support large communities such as Las Vegas, Barstow, Lancaster, Palmdale, Victorville, and St. George.</Review>
